It validates the project against all canonical checks, performs deeper structural analysis, fixes issues found, verifies the fixes pass, and only merges back on all-green.\n    24→\n    25→**Safety guarantee:** The main worktree is never modified until all checks pass in isolation.\n    26→\n    27→## Severity Levels\n    28→\n    29→Every finding is assigned a severity that determines handling:\n    30→\n    31→| Severity | Action | Description |\n    32→|----------|--------|-------------|\n    33→| **critical** | Abort loop | Structural integrity threat — cannot safely continue. Discard worktree. |\n    34→| **high** | Fix now | Must be resolved in this loop before proceeding to verify. |\n    35→| **medium** | Fix if time | Fix within remaining loop budget. Skip if loop cap approaching. |\n    36→| **low** | Log and skip | Record in report. No fix attempted. |\n    37→\n    38→Severity assignment rules:\n    39→- Protected-path violation → **critical**\n    40→- Test failure, broken hook, missing manifest entry → **high**\n    41→- Documentation drift, stale export, missing schema → **medium**\n    42→- Style issues, minor inconsistency, cosmetic → **low**\n    43→\n    44→## Quality Scoring\n    45→\n    46→Each loop measures a quality score **before** and **after** fixes:\n    47→\n    48→```\n    49→quality_score = (checks_passing / total_checks) * 100\n    50→```\n    51→\n    52→Track per loop:\n    53→- `quality_score_before` — score at start of loop (after Phase 1)\n    54→- `quality_score_after` — score at end of loop (after Phase 4 verify)\n    55→- `delta` — improvement from this loop's fixes\n    56→\n    57→**Effectiveness threshold:** If 3 consecutive loops show `delta < 2%`, the audit has converged — skip remaining loops.\n    58→\n    59→## Learning Integration\n    60→\n    61→After each audit loop, findings feed the learning pipeline:\n    62→\n    63→1. **Propose learnings:** For each finding category that appeared in this loop:\n    64→   - Check `state.sqlite` findings table for the same `finding_hash` in previous runs\n    65→   - If `recurrence_count >= 2`: auto-propose a learning to `memory/learnings/proposed/`\n    66→   - Learning scope tags: `scope_roles: [executor]`, `scope_concerns: [quality]`\n    67→2. **Store findings:** Insert all findings into `state.sqlite` via `insertFinding()` with severity and finding_hash\n    68→3. **Store audit record:** Insert `{run_id, finding_count, fix_count, manual_count, quality_score_before, quality_score_after}` into `audit_history`\n    69→\n    70→## Trend Tracking\n    71→\n    72→Before starting Loop 1, query previous audit results:\n    73→\n    74→```javascript\n    75→const trend = getAuditTrend(db, 5); // last 5 audits\n    76→```\n    77→\n    78→Present trend in the report:\n    79→- Are finding counts trending up or down?\n    80→- Are the same finding_hashes recurring? If so, the fixes aren't preventing recurrence — escalate.\n    81→- Has quality_score improved across runs?\n    82→\n    83→## Escalation Path\n    84→\n    85→Manual-required findings that cannot be auto-fixed are escalated:\n    86→\n    87→1. **Within the audit:** Logged in the report with remediation guidance\n    88→2. **Cross-run recurrence:** If the same manual finding recurs across 3+ audits, escalate to:\n    89→   - Create a task spec in `.wazir/runs/latest/tasks/` describing the fix\n    90→   - Flag in the audit report as **RECURRING — needs dedicated task**\n    91→3. **Critical findings:** Immediately logged. If 2+ critical findings in a single loop, abort the entire audit run.\n    92→\n    93→## Trigger\n    94→\n    95→On-demand: operator invokes `/self-audit` or requests a self-audit loop.\n    96→\n    97→### Parameters\n    98→\n    99→| Flag | Default | Max | Description |\n   100→|------|---------|-----|-------------|\n   101→| `--loops N` | 5 | 10 | Number of audit-fix loops to run. Each loop executes the full Phase 1-5 cycle. If a loop finds 0 new issues, subsequent loops are skipped (convergence detection). |\n   102→\n   103→## Worktree Isolation Model\n   104→\n   105→```\n   106→main worktree (untouched)\n   107→  └── agent spawns in isolated worktree (git worktree)\n   108→        ├── Phase 1: Validate (run all checks)\n   109→        ├── Phase 2: Deep audit (structural analysis)\n   110→        ├── Phase 3: Fix (remediate findings)\n   111→        ├── Phase 4: Verify (re-run all checks)\n   112→        └── Phase 5: Report (commit in worktree if green)\n   113→```\n   114→\n   115→If any Phase 4 check fails, the worktree is discarded — no changes reach main.\n   116→\n   117→## Phase 1: CLI Validation Sweep\n   118→\n   119→Run every validation check and capture results:\n   120→\n   121→```bash\n   122→node tooling/src/cli.js validate manifest\n   123→node tooling/src/cli.js validate hooks\n   124→node tooling/src/cli.js validate docs\n   125→node tooling/src/cli.js validate brand\n   126→node tooling/src/cli.js validate runtime\n   127→node tooling/src/cli.js validate changelog\n   128→node tooling/src/cli.js validate commits\n   129→node tooling/src/cli.js doctor --json\n   130→node tooling/src/cli.js export --check\n   131→```\n   132→\n   133→Collect pass/fail for each. Any failure is a finding. Assign severity per the severity table above.\n   134→\n   135→Calculate `quality_score_before` from the pass/fail results.\n   136→\n   137→## Phase 2: Deep Structural Audit\n   138→\n   139→Beyond CLI checks, inspect for:\n   140→\n   141→1. **Cross-reference consistency**\n   142→   - Every role in `wazir.manifest.yaml` has a file in `roles/`\n   143→   - Every workflow in manifest has a file in `workflows/`\n   144→   - Every skill directory has a `SKILL.md`\n   145→   - Every schema referenced in docs exists in `schemas/`\n   146→   - Composition map concerns reference existing expertise modules\n   147→\n   148→2. **Documentation drift**\n   149→   - `docs/architecture.md` component table matches actual directory structure\n   150→   - `docs/roles-and-workflows.md` role/workflow lists match manifest\n   151→   - README claims match actual project state\n   152→\n   153→3. **Export freshness**\n   154→   - Generated exports match canonical sources (via `export --check`)\n   155→   - Host export directories contain expected structure\n   156→\n   157→4. **Schema coverage**\n   158→   - Every workflow that produces artifacts has a corresponding schema\n   159→   - Schema files are valid JSON\n   160→\n   161→5. **Hook integrity**\n   162→   - Hook scripts referenced in `.claude/settings.json` exist and are executable\n   163→   - Hook definitions in `hooks/definitions/` cover all manifest-required hooks\n   164→\n   165→6. **Skill structure**\n   166→   - Each skill dir under `skills/` has a well-formed `SKILL.md` with frontmatter\n   167→   - Skills referenced in documentation actually exist\n   168→\n   169→7. **Code Quality**\n   170→   - Run `node tooling/src/cli.js validate` (all subcommands) and capture exit codes\n   171→   - If `eslint` is present in `package.json` scripts or devDependencies, run `npx eslint .` and capture results\n   172→   - If `tsc` is present in `package.json` scripts or devDependencies, run `npx tsc --noEmit` and capture results\n   173→   - Tools not found in `package.json` are skipped with a note in the report\n   174→\n   175→8. **Test Coverage**\n   176→   - Run `npm test` and capture pass/fail counts from output\n   177→   - Any test failure is a finding\n   178→\n   179→9. **Expertise Coverage**\n   180→   - Read `expertise/composition-map.yaml`\n   181→   - For every module path referenced, check that the file exists under `expertise/`\n   182→   - Missing files are findings\n   183→\n   184→10. **Export Freshness**\n   185→    - Run `wazir export --check`\n   186→    - Any drift detected is a finding\n   187→\n   188→11. **Input Coverage** (run-scoped — only when a run directory exists)\n   189→    - Read the original input file(s) from `.wazir/input/` or `.wazir/runs/<id>/sources/`\n   190→    - Read the execution plan from `.wazir/runs/<id>/clarified/execution-plan.md`\n   191→    - Read the actual commits on the branch: `git log --oneline main..HEAD`\n   192→    - Build a coverage matrix: every distinct item in the input should map to:\n   193→      - At least one task in the execution plan\n   194→      - At least one commit in the git log\n   195→    - **Missing items** (in input but not in plan AND not in commits) → **HIGH** severity finding\n   196→    - **Partial items** (in plan but no corresponding commit) → **MEDIUM** severity finding\n   197→    - **Fully covered items** (input → plan → commit) → pass\n   198→    - Output the coverage matrix in the audit report:\n   199→      ```\n   200→      | Input Item | Plan Task | Commit | Status |\n   201→      |------------|-----------|--------|--------|\n   202→      | Item 1     | Task 3    | abc123 | PASS   |\n   203→      | Item 2     | Task 5    | —      | PARTIAL|\n   204→      | Item 3     | —         | —      | MISSING|\n   205→      ```\n   206→    - This dimension catches scope reduction AFTER the fact — a safety net for when the clarifier or planner fails\n   207→\n   208→## Protected-Path Safety Rails\n   209→\n   210→Before applying ANY fix in Phase 3, check if the target file is in a protected path. The self-audit loop MUST NOT modify files in:\n   211→\n   212→- `skills/`\n   213→- `workflows/`\n   214→- `roles/`\n   215→- `schemas/`\n   216→- `wazir.manifest.yaml`\n   217→- `docs/concepts/`\n   218→- `docs/reference/`\n   219→- `expertise/composition-map.yaml`\n   220→- `docs/plans/`\n   221→- `program.md`\n   222→\n   223→If a fix would touch a protected path, log it as a **manual-required** finding and skip. If `git diff --name-only` shows any protected path was modified during a loop iteration, **ABORT** the loop and discard the worktree.\n   224→\n   225→## Phase 3: Fix\n   226→\n   227→For each finding from Phases 1-2, ordered by severity (critical first):\n   228→\n   229→1. **Critical findings:** Abort immediately. Discard worktree. Report the critical finding.\n   230→2. **High findings:** Must fix now.\n   231→3. **Medium findings:** Fix if loop budget allows (remaining loops > 1).\n   232→4. **Low findings:** Log only. No fix attempted.\n   233→\n   234→For high/medium findings:\n   235→1. Categorize as **auto-fixable** or **manual-required**\n   236→2. Auto-fixable issues: apply the fix directly\n   237→   - Missing files → create stubs or fix references\n   238→   - Stale exports → run `export build`\n   239→   - Documentation drift → update docs to match reality\n   240→   - Permission issues → `chmod +x` hook scripts\n   241→   - Schema formatting → auto-format\n   242→3. Manual-required issues: document in the audit report with remediation guidance. Check escalation path for recurrence.\n   243→\n   244→**Fix constraints:**\n   245→- Never modify `input/` (read-only operator surface)\n   246→- Prefer updating docs to match code (code is truth) unless the code is clearly wrong\n   247→- Keep fixes minimal — one concern per change\n   248→\n   249→## Phase 4: Verify\n   250→\n   251→Re-run the entire Phase 1 validation sweep. All checks must pass.\n   252→\n   253→If any check fails after fixes:\n   254→- Revert the failing fix\n   255→- Document the revert and the root cause\n   256→- Re-verify\n   257→\n   258→## Phase 5: Report, Learn & Commit\n   259→\n   260→### Quality Score\n   261→\n   262→Re-run Phase 1 checks and calculate `quality_score_after`. Compute delta.\n   263→\n   264→### Learning Extraction\n   265→\n   266→1. Hash each finding description → `finding_hash`\n   267→2. Store all findings in `state.sqlite` via `insertFinding(db, {run_id, phase: 'self-audit', source: 'self-audit', severity, description, finding_hash})`\n   268→3. Query `getRecurringFindingHashes(db, 2)` — findings occurring 2+ times across runs\n   269→4. For each recurring finding not already in `memory/learnings/proposed/`:\n   270→   - Write a learning proposal: `memory/learnings/proposed/self-audit-<hash-prefix>.md`\n   271→   - Content: what the issue is, how often it recurs, recommended prevention\n   272→5. Store audit record: `insertAuditRecord(db, {run_id, finding_count, fix_count, manual_count, quality_score_before, quality_score_after})`\n   273→\n   274→### Report\n   275→\n   276→Produce a structured report:\n   277→\n   278→```markdown\n   279→# Self-Audit Report — Loop N — <date>\n   280→\n   281→## Quality Score\n   282→- Before: X% → After: Y% (delta: +Z%)\n   283→\n   284→## Trend (last 5 audits)\n   285→| Run | Date | Findings | Fixes | Quality |\n   286→|-----|------|----------|-------|---------|\n   287→| ... | ...  | ...      | ...   | ...     |\n   288→\n   289→## Validation Sweep\n   290→| Check | Severity | Before | After |\n   291→|-------|----------|--------|-------|\n   292→| manifest | high | PASS/FAIL | PASS |\n   293→| hooks | high | PASS/FAIL | PASS |\n   294→| ... | ... | ... | ... |\n   295→\n   296→## Findings by Severity\n   297→### Critical (N) — loop aborted if any\n   298→### High (N) — fixed\n   299→### Medium (N) — fixed if budget allowed\n   300→### Low (N) — logged only\n   301→\n   302→## Auto-Fixed (N)\n   303→- [F-001] [high] <description> — fixed by <change>\n   304→- ...\n   305→\n   306→## Manual Required (N)\n   307→- [M-001] [medium] <description> — remediation: <guidance>\n   308→- [M-002] [medium] <description> — **RECURRING (3x)** — needs dedicated task\n   309→- ...\n   310→\n   311→## Proposed Learnings (N)\n   312→- <learning-file>: <summary>\n   313→- ...\n   314→\n   315→## Changes Made\n   316→- <file>: <what changed>\n   317→- ...\n   318→\n   319→## Verification\n   320→All checks: PASS/FAIL\n   321→```\n   322→\n   323→If all checks pass, commit changes in the worktree with:\n   324→```\n   325→fix(self-audit): loop N — <summary of fixes>\n   326→```\n   327→\n   328→The worktree agent returns its results. If changes were made, the caller can merge them.\n   329→\n   330→## Loop Behavior\n   331→\n   332→Default: **5 loops** (override with `--loops N`, max 10).\n   333→\n   334→When running multiple loops:\n   335→- Loop 1 audits the current state, fixes what it finds\n   336→- Loop 2 audits the result of Loop 1, catches anything missed or introduced\n   337→- Each loop is independent and runs in its own fresh worktree\n   338→- **Convergence detection:** if Loop N finds **0 new issues** (no new findings beyond what previous loops already reported), all subsequent loops are skipped and the audit terminates early\n   339→- **Effectiveness convergence:** if 3 consecutive loops show `quality_score delta < 2%`, skip remaining loops\n   340→- **Critical abort:** if any loop encounters 2+ critical findings, abort the entire audit run\n   341→- If a loop modifies a protected path (see Protected-Path Safety Rails above), the loop is aborted and the worktree is discarded\n   342→\n   343→The final branch is **NOT auto-merged** — it requires human review.\n   344→\n   345→## State Database Integration\n   346→\n   347→The self-audit skill requires `state.sqlite` (see `tooling/src/state/db.js`). At audit start:\n   348→\n   349→```javascript\n   350→const { openStateDb, getAuditTrend, insertFinding, insertAuditRecord, getRecurringFindingHashes } = require('../../tooling/src/state/db');\n   351→const db = openStateDb(stateRoot);\n   352→```\n   353→\n   354→All findings are persisted across runs, enabling trend detection and learning extraction.\n   355→"}]},"uuid":"8773763d-8f1f-405f-9039-13cc3058e1d1","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:38:18.418Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e105742b-2ba9-40e8-94e0-03703ca5e6b6","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

Resume or start fresh?\"\n   181→- **Options:**\n   182→  1. \"Resume from the last completed phase\" *(Recommended)*\n   183→  2. \"Start fresh with a new empty run\"\n   184→\n   185→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   186→\n   187→**If Resume:**\n   188→- Copy `clarified/` from previous run into new run, EXCEPT `user-feedback.md`.\n   189→- Detect last completed phase by checking which artifacts exist.\n   190→- **Staleness check:** If input files are newer than copied artifacts, warn and offer to re-run clarification.\n   191→\n   192→## Step 4: Build Run Config\n   193→\n   194→**No questions asked.** Depth, intent, and mode are all inferred or defaulted.\n   195→\n   196→### Intent Inference\n   197→\n   198→Infer intent from the request text using keyword matching:\n   199→\n   200→| Keywords in request | Inferred Intent |\n   201→|-------------------|-----------------|\n   202→| fix, bug, broken, crash, error, issue, wrong | `bugfix` |\n   203→| refactor, clean, restructure, reorganize, rename, simplify | `refactor` |\n   204→| doc, document, readme, guide, explain | `docs` |\n   205→| research, spike, explore, investigate, prototype | `spike` |\n   206→| (anything else) | `feature` |\n   207→\n   208→Depth defaults to `standard`. Override only via inline modifiers (`/wazir quick ...`, `/wazir deep ...`).\n   209→\n   210→### Write Run Config\n   211→\n   212→Save to `.wazir/runs/<run-id>/run-config.yaml`:\n   213→\n   214→```yaml\n   215→run_id: run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS\n   216→parent_run_id: null\n   217→continuation_reason: null\n   218→\n   219→request: \"the original user request\"\n   220→request_summary: \"short summary\"\n   221→parsed_intent: feature\n   222→entry_point: \"/wazir\"\n   223→\n   224→depth: standard\n   225→interaction_mode: guided  # auto | guided | interactive\n   226→\n   227→# Workflow policy — individual workflows within each phase\n   228→workflow_policy:\n   229→  # Clarifier phase workflows\n   230→  discover:       { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   231→  clarify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   232→  specify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   233→  spec-challenge: { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   234→  author:         { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   235→  design:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   236→  design-review:  { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   237→  plan:           { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   238→  plan-review:    { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   239→  # Executor phase workflows\n   240→  execute:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   241→  verify:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   242→  # Final Review phase workflows\n   243→  review:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   244→  learn:          { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   245→  prepare_next:   { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   246→  run_audit:      { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   247→\n   248→research_topics: []\n   249→\n   250→created_at: \"YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ\"\n   251→completed_at: null\n   252→```\n   253→\n   254→### Workflow Skip Rules\n   255→\n   256→Map intent + depth to applicable workflows. The system decides — the user does NOT pick.\n   257→\n   258→| Class | Workflows | Rules |\n   259→|-------|-----------|-------|\n   260→| **Core** (always run) | `clarify`, `execute`, `verify`, `review` | Never skipped |\n   261→| **Adaptive** (run when evidence says so) | `discover`, `design`, `author`, `specify` | Skipped for bugfix/docs/spike at quick depth |\n   262→| **Scale** (intensity varies) | `spec-challenge`, `plan-review`, `design-review` | Loop cap controls iteration depth |\n   263→| **Post-run** (always run) | `learn`, `prepare_next` | Part of Final Review phase |\n   264→\n   265→Log skip decisions with reasons in `workflow_policy`.\n   266→\n   267→### Confidence Gate\n   268→\n   269→After building run config:\n   270→\n   271→- **High confidence** — one-line summary and proceed:\n   272→  > **Running: standard depth, feature, sequential. Proceeding...**\n   273→\n   274→- **Low confidence** — show plan and ask:\n   275→\n   276→  Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   277→  - **Question:** \"Does this run configuration look right?\"\n   278→  - **Options:**\n   279→    1. \"Yes, proceed\" *(Recommended)*\n   280→    2. \"No, let me adjust\"\n   281→\n   282→  Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   283→\n   284→```bash\n   285→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase init --status completed\n   286→```\n   287→\n   288→Run the phase report and display it to the user:\n   289→```bash\n   290→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase init\n   291→```\n   292→\n   293→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   294→\n   295→---\n   296→\n   297→# Interaction Modes\n   298→\n   299→The `interaction_mode` field in run-config controls how the pipeline interacts with the user:\n   300→\n   301→| Mode | Inline modifier | Behavior | Best for |\n   302→|------|----------------|----------|----------|\n   303→| **`guided`** | (default) | Pipeline runs, pauses at phase checkpoints for user approval. Current default behavior. | Most work |\n   304→| **`auto`** | `/wazir auto ...` | No human checkpoints. Codex reviews all. Gating agent decides continue/loop_back/escalate. Stops ONLY on escalate. | Overnight, clear spec, well-understood domain |\n   305→| **`interactive`** | `/wazir interactive ...` | More questions, more discussion, co-designs with user. Researcher presents options. Executor checks approach before coding. | Ambiguous requirements, new domain, learning |\n   306→\n   307→## `auto` mode constraints\n   308→\n   309→- **Codex REQUIRED** — refuse to start auto mode if `multi_tool.codex` is not configured in `.wazir/state/config.json`. Error: \"Auto mode requires an external reviewer (Codex). Configure it first or use guided mode.\"\n   310→- **On escalate:** STOP immediately, write the escalation reason to `.wazir/runs/<id>/escalations/`, and wait for user input\n   311→- **Wall-clock limit:** default 4 hours. If exceeded, stop with escalation.\n   312→- **Never auto-commits to main** — always work on feature branch\n   313→- All checkpoints (AskUserQuestion) are skipped — gating agent evaluates phase reports and decides\n   314→\n   315→## `guided` mode (default)\n   316→\n   317→Current behavior — no changes needed. Checkpoints at phase boundaries, user approves before advancing.\n   318→\n   319→## `interactive` mode\n   320→\n   321→- **Clarifier:** asks more detailed questions, presents research findings with options: \"I found 3 approaches — which interests you?\"\n   322→- **Executor:** checks approach before coding: \"I'm about to implement auth with Supabase — sound right?\"\n   323→- **Reviewer:** discusses findings with user, not just presents verdict: \"I found a potential auth bypass — here's why I think it's high severity, do you agree?\"\n   324→- Slower but highest quality for complex/ambiguous work\n   325→\n   326→## Mode checking in phase skills\n   327→\n   328→All phase skills check `interaction_mode` from run-config at every checkpoint:\n   329→\n   330→```\n   331→# Read from run-config\n   332→interaction_mode = run_config.interaction_mode ?? 'guided'\n   333→\n   334→# At each checkpoint:\n   335→if interaction_mode == 'auto':\n   336→    # Skip checkpoint, let gating agent decide\n   337→elif interaction_mode == 'interactive':\n   338→    # More detailed question, present options, discuss\n   339→else:\n   340→    # guided — standard checkpoint with AskUserQuestion\n   341→```\n   342→\n   343→---\n   344→\n   345→# Two-Level Phase Model\n   346→\n   347→The pipeline has 4 top-level **phases**, each containing multiple **workflows** with review loops:\n   348→\n   349→```\n   350→Phase 1: Init\n   351→  └── (inline — no sub-workflows)\n   352→\n   353→Phase 2: Clarifier\n   354→  ├── discover (research) ← research-review loop\n   355→  ├── clarify ← clarification-review loop\n   356→  ├── specify ← spec-challenge loop\n   357→  ├── author (adaptive) ← approval gate\n   358→  ├── design ← design-review loop\n   359→  └── plan ← plan-review loop\n   360→\n   361→Phase 3: Executor\n   362→  ├── execute (per-task) ← task-review loop per task\n   363→  └── verify\n   364→\n   365→Phase 4: Final Review\n   366→  ├── review (final) ← scored review\n   367→  ├── learn\n   368→  └── prepare_next\n   369→```\n   370→\n   371→**Event capture uses both levels.** When emitting phase events, include `--parent-phase`:\n   372→```bash\n   373→wazir capture event --run <id> --event phase_enter --phase discover --parent-phase clarifier --status in_progress\n   374→```\n   375→\n   376→**Progress markers between workflows:** After each workflow completes, output:\n   377→> Phase 2: Clarifier > Workflow: specify (3 of 6 workflows complete)\n   378→\n   379→**`wazir status` shows both levels:** \"Phase 2: Clarifier > Workflow: specify\"\n   380→\n   381→---\n   382→\n   383→# Phase 2: Clarifier\n   384→\n   385→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   386→\n   387→> **Clarifier Phase** — About to research your codebase, clarify requirements, harden the spec, brainstorm designs, and produce an execution plan.\n   388→>\n   389→> **Why this matters:** Without this, I'd guess your tech stack, misunderstand constraints, miss edge cases in the spec, and build the wrong architecture. Every ambiguity left unresolved here becomes a bug or rework cycle later.\n   390→>\n   391→> **Looking for:** Unstated assumptions, scope boundaries, conflicting requirements, missing acceptance criteria\n   392→\n   393→```bash\n   394→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_enter --phase clarifier --status in_progress\n   395→```\n   396→\n   397→Invoke the `wz:clarifier` skill. It handles all sub-workflows internally:\n   398→\n   399→1. **Source Capture** — fetch URLs from input\n   400→2. **Research** (discover workflow) — codebase + external research\n   401→3. **Clarify** (clarify workflow) — scope, constraints, assumptions\n   402→4. **Spec Harden** (specify + spec-challenge workflows) — measurable spec\n   403→5. **Brainstorm** (design + design-review workflows) — design approaches\n   404→6. **Plan** (plan + plan-review workflows) — execution plan\n   405→\n   406→Each sub-workflow has its own review loop. User checkpoints between major steps.\n   407→\n   408→### Scope Invariant\n   409→\n   410→**Hard rule:** `items_in_plan >= items_in_input` unless the user explicitly approves scope reduction. The clarifier MUST NOT autonomously tier, defer, or drop items from the user's input. It can suggest prioritization, but the decision belongs to the user.\n   411→\n   412→Output: approved spec + design + execution plan in `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/`.\n   413→\n   414→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   415→\n   416→> **Clarifier Phase complete.**\n   417→>\n   418→> **Found:** [N] ambiguities resolved, [N] assumptions made explicit, [N] scope boundaries drawn, [N] acceptance criteria hardened\n   419→>\n   420→> **Without this phase:** Requirements would be interpreted differently across tasks, acceptance criteria would be vague and untestable, the design would be ad-hoc, and the plan would miss dependency ordering\n   421→>\n   422→> **Changed because of this work:** [List spec tightening changes, resolved questions, design decisions, scope adjustments]\n   423→\n   424→```bash\n   425→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase clarifier --status completed\n   426→```\n   427→\n   428→Run the phase report and display savings to the user:\n   429→```bash\n   430→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase clarifier\n   431→wazir stats --run <run-id>\n   432→```\n   433→\n   434→**Show savings in conversation output:**\n   435→> **Context savings this phase:** Used wazir index for [N] queries and context-mode for [M] commands, saving ~[X] tokens ([Y]% reduction). Without these, this phase would have consumed [A] tokens instead of [B].\n   436→\n   437→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   438→\n   439→---\n   440→\n   441→# Phase 3: Executor\n   442→\n   443→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   444→\n   445→> **Executor Phase** — About to implement [N] tasks in dependency order with TDD (test-first), per-task code review, and verification before each commit.\n   446→>\n   447→> **Why this matters:** Without this discipline, tests get skipped, edge cases get missed, integration points break silently, and review catches problems too late when they're expensive to fix.\n   448→>\n   449→> **Looking for:** Correct dependency ordering, test coverage for each task, clean per-task review passes, no implementation drift from the approved plan\n   450→\n   451→## Phase Gate (Hard Gate)\n   452→\n   453→Before entering the Executor phase, verify ALL clarifier artifacts exist:\n   454→\n   455→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/clarification.md`\n   456→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/spec-hardened.md`\n   457→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/design.md`\n   458→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/execution-plan.md`\n   459→\n   460→If ANY file is missing, **STOP**:\n   461→\n   462→> **Cannot enter Executor phase: missing prerequisite artifacts from Clarifier.**\n   463→>\n   464→> Missing: [list missing files]\n   465→>\n   466→> The Clarifier phase must complete before execution can begin. Run `/wazir:clarifier` first.\n   467→\n   468→**Do NOT skip this check. Do NOT rationalize that the input is \"clear enough\" to bypass clarification. Every pipeline run must produce these artifacts.**\n   469→\n   470→```bash\n   471→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_enter --phase executor --status in_progress\n   472→```\n   473→\n   474→**Pre-execution gate:**\n   475→\n   476→```bash\n   477→wazir validate manifest && wazir validate hooks\n   478→# Hard gate — stop if either fails.\n   479→```\n   480→\n   481→Invoke the `wz:executor` skill. It handles:\n   482→\n   483→1. **Execute** (execute workflow) — per-task TDD cycle with review before each commit\n   484→2. **Verify** (verify workflow) — deterministic verification of all claims\n   485→\n   486→Per-task review: `--mode task-review`, 5 task-execution dimensions.\n   487→Tasks always run sequentially.\n   488→\n   489→Output: code changes + verification proof in `.wazir/runs/latest/artifacts/`.\n   490→\n   491→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   492→\n   493→> **Executor Phase complete.**\n   494→>\n   495→> **Found:** [N]/[N] tasks implemented, [N] tests written, [N] per-task review passes completed, [N] findings fixed before commit\n   496→>\n   497→> **Without this phase:** Code would ship without tests, review findings would accumulate until final review (10x more expensive to fix), and verification claims would be unsubstantiated\n   498→>\n   499→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of commits with conventional commit messages, test counts, verification evidence collected]\n   500→\n   501→```bash\n   502→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase executor --status completed\n   503→```\n   504→\n   505→Run the phase report and display savings to the user:\n   506→```bash\n   507→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase executor\n   508→wazir stats --run <run-id>\n   509→```\n   510→\n   511→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   512→\n   513→**Show savings in conversation output:**\n   514→> **Context savings this phase:** Used wazir index for [N] queries and context-mode for [M] commands, saving ~[X] tokens ([Y]% reduction).\n   515→\n   516→---\n   517→\n   518→# Phase 4: Final Review\n   519→\n   520→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   521→\n   522→> **Final Review Phase** — About to run adversarial 7-dimension review comparing the implementation against your original input, extract durable learnings, and prepare the handoff.\n   523→>\n   524→> **Why this matters:** Without this, implementation drift ships undetected, missing acceptance criteria go unnoticed, untested code paths hide bugs, and the same mistakes repeat in the next run.\n   525→>\n   526→> **Looking for:** Spec violations, missing features, dead code paths, unsubstantiated claims, scope creep, security gaps, stale documentation\n   527→\n   528→## Phase Gate (Hard Gate)\n   529→\n   530→Before entering the Final Review phase, verify the Executor produced its proof:\n   531→\n   532→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/artifacts/verification-proof.md`\n   533→\n   534→If missing, **STOP**:\n   535→\n   536→> **Cannot enter Final Review: missing verification proof from Executor.**\n   537→>\n   538→> The Executor phase must complete and produce `verification-proof.md` before final review. Run `/wazir:executor` first.\n   539→\n   540→```bash\n   541→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_enter --phase final_review --status in_progress\n   542→```\n   543→\n   544→This phase validates the implementation against the **ORIGINAL INPUT** (not the task specs — the executor's per-task reviewer already covered that).\n   545→\n   546→### 4a: Review (reviewer role in final mode)\n   547→\n   548→Invoke `wz:reviewer --mode final`.\n   549→7-dimension scored review comparing implementation against the original user input.\n   550→Score 0-70. Verdicts: PASS (56+), NEEDS MINOR FIXES (42-55), NEEDS REWORK (28-41), FAIL (0-27).\n   551→\n   552→### 4b: Learn (learner role)\n   553→\n   554→Extract durable learnings from the completed run:\n   555→- Scan all review findings (internal + Codex)\n   556→- Propose learnings to `memory/learnings/proposed/`\n   557→- Findings that recur across 2+ runs → auto-proposed as learnings\n   558→- Learnings require explicit scope tags (roles, stacks, concerns)\n   559→\n   560→**Learn workflow completion guard:** If `workflow_policy.learn.enabled: true` in run config AND no files exist in `memory/learnings/proposed/` matching the current run ID pattern (`run-<current-id>-*.md`): log a warning finding: 'Learn workflow enabled but no proposed learnings written for this run'. This ensures the learn workflow always produces output when enabled.\n   561→\n   562→### 4c: Prepare Next (planner role)\n   563→\n   564→Prepare context and handoff for the next run:\n   565→- Write handoff document\n   566→- Compress/archive unneeded files\n   567→- Record what's left to do\n   568→\n   569→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   570→\n   571→> **Final Review Phase complete.**\n   572→>\n   573→> **Found:** [N] findings across 7 dimensions, [N] blocking issues, [N] warnings, [N] learnings proposed for future runs\n   574→>\n   575→> **Without this phase:** Implementation drift from the original request would ship undetected, untested paths would hide production bugs, and recurring mistakes would never get captured as learnings\n   576→>\n   577→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of findings fixed, score achieved, learnings extracted, handoff prepared]\n   578→\n   579→```bash\n   580→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase final_review --status completed\n   581→```\n   582→\n   583→Run the phase report and display it to the user:\n   584→```bash\n   585→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase final_review\n   586→```\n   587→\n   588→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   589→\n   590→---\n   591→\n   592→## Step 5: CHANGELOG + Gitflow Validation (Hard Gates)\n   593→\n   594→Before presenting results:\n   595→\n   596→```bash\n   597→wazir validate changelog --require-entries --base main\n   598→wazir validate commits --base main\n   599→```\n   600→\n   601→Both must pass before PR. These are not warnings.\n   602→\n   603→## Step 6: Present Results\n   604→\n   605→After the reviewer completes, present verdict with numbered options:\n   606→\n   607→### If PASS (score 56+):\n   608→\n   609→> **Result: PASS (score/70)**\n   610→\n   611→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   612→- **Question:** \"Pipeline passed. What would you like to do next?\"\n   613→- **Options:**\n   614→  1. \"Create a PR\" *(Recommended)*\n   615→  2. \"Merge directly\"\n   616→  3. \"Review the changes first\"\n   617→\n   618→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   619→\n   620→### If NEEDS MINOR FIXES (score 42-55):\n   621→\n   622→> **Result: NEEDS MINOR FIXES (score/70)**\n   623→\n   624→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   625→- **Question:** \"Minor issues found. How should we handle them?\"\n   626→- **Options:**\n   627→  1. \"Auto-fix and re-review\" *(Recommended)*\n   628→  2. \"Fix manually\"\n   629→  3. \"Accept as-is\"\n   630→\n   631→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   632→\n   633→### If NEEDS REWORK (score 28-41):\n   634→\n   635→> **Result: NEEDS REWORK (score/70)**\n   636→\n   637→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   638→- **Question:** \"Significant issues found. How should we proceed?\"\n   639→- **Options:**\n   640→  1. \"Re-run affected tasks\" *(Recommended)*\n   641→  2. \"Review findings in detail\"\n   642→  3. \"Abandon this run\"\n   643→\n   644→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   645→\n   646→### If FAIL (score 0-27):\n   647→\n   648→> **Result: FAIL (score/70)**\n   649→>\n   650→> Something fundamental went wrong. Review the findings above.\n   651→\n   652→### Run Summary\n   653→\n   654→```bash\n   655→wazir capture summary --run <run-id>\n   656→wazir status --run <run-id> --json\n   657→```\n   658→\n   659→## Error Handling\n   660→\n   661→If any phase fails:\n   662→\n   663→> **Phase [name] failed: [reason]**\n   664→\n   665→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   666→- **Question:** \"Phase [name] failed: [reason]. How should we proceed?\"\n   667→- **Options:**\n   668→  1. \"Retry this phase\" *(Recommended)*\n   669→  2. \"Skip and continue\" *(only if workflows within phase are adaptive)*\n   670→  3. \"Abort the run\"\n   671→\n   672→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   673→\n   674→---\n   675→\n   676→# Audit Mode\n   677→\n   678→Triggered by `/wazir audit` or `/wazir audit <focus>`.\n   679→\n   680→Runs a structured codebase audit. Invokes the `run-audit` skill.\n   681→\n   682→Parse inline audit types: `/wazir audit security` → skip Question 1.\n   683→\n   684→After audit:\n   685→\n   686→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   687→- **Question:** \"Audit complete. What would you like to do with the findings?\"\n   688→- **Options:**\n   689→  1. \"Review the findings\" *(Recommended)*\n   690→  2. \"Generate a fix plan\"\n   691→  3. \"Run the pipeline on the fix plan\"\n   692→\n   693→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   694→\n   695→If option 3, save findings as briefing and run pipeline with intent = `bugfix`.\n   696→\n   697→---\n   698→\n   699→# PRD Mode\n   700→\n   701→Triggered by `/wazir prd` or `/wazir prd <run-id>`.\n   702→\n   703→Generates a PRD from a completed run. Reads approved design, task specs, execution plan, review results. Saves to `docs/prd/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-prd.md`.\n   704→\n   705→After generation:\n   706→\n   707→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   708→- **Question:** \"PRD generated. What would you like to do?\"\n   709→- **Options:**\n   710→  1. \"Review the PRD\" *(Recommended)*\n   711→  2. \"Commit it\"\n   712→  3. \"Edit before committing\"\n   713→\n   714→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   715→\n   716→---\n   717→\n   718→## Reasoning Chain Output\n   719→\n   720→Every phase produces reasoning output at two layers:\n   721→\n   722→### Layer 1: Conversation Output (concise — for the user)\n   723→\n   724→Before each major decision, output one trigger sentence and one reasoning sentence:\n   725→\n   726→> \"Your request mentions 'overnight autonomous run' — researching how Devin and Karpathy's autoresearch handle this, because unattended runs need different safety constraints than interactive ones.\"\n   727→\n   728→After each phase, output what was found and a counterfactual:\n   729→\n   730→> \"Found: you use Supabase auth (not custom JWT). If I'd skipped research, I would have built JWT middleware — completely wrong.\"\n   731→\n   732→### Layer 2: File Output (detailed — for learning and reports)\n   733→\n   734→Save full reasoning chain to `.wazir/runs/<id>/reasoning/phase-<name>-reasoning.md` with entries:\n   735→\n   736→```markdown\n   737→### Decision: [title]\n   738→- **Trigger:** What prompted this decision\n   739→- **Options considered:** List of alternatives\n   740→- **Chosen:** The selected option\n   741→- **Reasoning:** Why this option was chosen\n   742→- **Confidence:** high | medium | low\n   743→- **Counterfactual:** What would have gone wrong without this information\n   744→```\n   745→\n   746→Create the `reasoning/` directory during run init. Every phase skill (clarifier, executor, reviewer) writes its own reasoning file. Counterfactuals appear in BOTH conversation output AND reasoning files.\n   747→\n   748→## Interaction Rules\n   749→\n   750→- **One question at a time** — never combine multiple questions\n   751→- **Numbered options** — always present choices as numbered lists\n   752→- **Mark defaults** — always show \"(Recommended)\" on the suggested option\n   753→- **Wait for answer** — never proceed past a question until the user responds\n   754→- **No open-ended questions** — every question has concrete options to pick from\n   755→- **Inline answers accepted** — users can type the number or the option name\n   756→"}]},"uuid":"8b0624bf-1761-47e4-b335-79bb82875b85","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:38:18.423Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b4d6f61a-31e9-4581-b5a4-11487d89f2c5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

If no index exists: `wazir index build && wazir index summarize --tier all`\n    20→\n    21→Run the Clarifier phase — everything from reading input to having an approved execution plan.\n    22→\n    23→**Pacing rule:** This skill has mandatory user checkpoints between sub-workflows. Do NOT skip checkpoints. Do NOT combine sub-workflows. Complete each fully, present output, and wait for explicit user approval before advancing.\n    24→\n    25→Review loops follow the pattern in `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md`. Check `.wazir/state/config.json` exists. If not, run `wazir init` first.\n    32→2. Check `.wazir/input/briefing.md` exists. If not, ask the user what they want to build and save it there.\n    33→3. Scan `input/` (project-level) and `.wazir/input/` (state-level) for additional input files. Present what's found.\n    34→4. Read config for `default_depth` and `multi_tool` settings.\n    35→5. **Load accepted learnings:**\n    36→   1. Glob `memory/learnings/accepted/*.md`\n    37→   2. Match scope tags against current run's intent (from run config `parsed_intent`) and detected stack (from research findings or `config.json` stack settings)\n    39→   4. Inject matching learnings into context, sorted by confidence (highest first), most recent first, limit 10\n    40→   5. If no accepted learnings exist or no matches found: skip silently — this is expected until the pipeline matures\n    41→6. Create a run directory if one doesn't exist:\n    42→   ```bash\n    43→   mkdir -p .wazir/runs/run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/{sources,tasks,artifacts,reviews,clarified}\n    44→   ln -sfn run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS .wazir/runs/latest\n    45→   ```\n    46→\n    47→---\n    48→\n    49→## Context-Mode Usage\n    50→\n    51→Read `context_mode` from `.wazir/state/config.json`:\n    52→\n    53→- **If `context_mode.enabled: true`:** Use `fetch_and_index` for URL fetching, `search` for follow-up queries on indexed content. Use `execute` or `execute_file` for large outputs instead of Bash.\n    54→- **If `context_mode.enabled: false`:** Fall back to `WebFetch` for URLs and `Bash` for commands.\n    55→\n    56→---\n    57→\n    58→## Sub-Workflow 1: Research (discover workflow)\n    59→\n    60→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n    61→\n    62→> **Research** — About to scan the codebase and fetch external references to understand the existing architecture, tech stack, and any standards referenced in the briefing.\n    63→>\n    64→> **Why this matters:** Without research, I'd assume the wrong framework version, miss existing patterns in the codebase, and contradict established conventions. Every wrong assumption here cascades into a wrong spec and wrong implementation.\n    65→>\n    66→> **Looking for:** Existing code patterns, dependency versions, external standard definitions, architectural constraints\n    67→\n    68→Delegate to the discover workflow (`workflows/discover.md`):\n    69→\n    70→1. **Keyword extraction:** Read the briefing and extract concepts/terms that are vague, reference external standards, or use unfamiliar terminology.\n    71→   - **When to research:** concept references an external standard by name, uses a tool/library not seen in the codebase, or is ambiguous enough that two agents could interpret it differently.\n    72→   - **When NOT to research:** concept is fully defined in the input, or it's a well-known programming concept.\n    73→2. **Fetch sources:** For each concept needing research:\n    74→   - Use `fetch_and_index` (if context-mode available) or `WebFetch` to fetch the source.\n    75→   - Save fetched content to `.wazir/runs/latest/sources/`.\n    76→   - Track each fetch in `sources/manifest.json`.\n    77→3. **Error handling:** 404/unreachable → log failure, continue. Research is best-effort.\n    78→4. The **researcher role** produces the research artifact.\n    79→5. The **reviewer role** runs the research-review loop with `--mode research-review`.\n    80→6. Loop runs for `pass_counts[depth]` passes.\n    81→\n    82→Save result to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/research-brief.md`.\n    83→\n    84→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n    85→\n    86→> **Research complete.**\n    87→>\n    88→> **Found:** [N] external sources fetched, [N] codebase patterns identified, [N] architectural constraints documented\n    89→>\n    90→> **Without this phase:** Spec would be built on assumptions instead of evidence — wrong framework APIs, missed existing utilities, contradicted naming conventions\n    91→>\n    92→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of key discoveries — e.g., \"found existing auth middleware at src/middleware/auth.ts\", \"project uses Vitest not Jest\"]\n    93→\n    94→### Checkpoint: Research Review\n    95→\n    96→> **Research complete. Here's what I found:**\n    97→>\n    98→> [Summary of codebase state, relevant architecture, external context]\n    99→\n   100→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   101→- **Question:** \"Does the research look complete and accurate?\"\n   102→- **Options:**\n   103→  1. \"Looks good, continue\" *(Recommended)*\n   104→  2. \"Missing context — let me add more information\"\n   105→  3. \"Wrong direction — let me clarify the intent\"\n   106→\n   107→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   108→\n   109→---\n   110→\n   111→## Sub-Workflow 2: Clarify (clarify workflow)\n   112→\n   113→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   114→\n   115→> **Clarification** — About to transform the briefing and research into a precise scope document with explicit constraints, assumptions, and boundaries.\n   116→>\n   117→> **Why this matters:** Without explicit clarification, \"add user auth\" could mean OAuth, magic links, or username/password. Every ambiguity left here becomes a 50/50 coin flip during implementation that could produce the wrong feature.\n   118→>\n   119→> **Looking for:** Ambiguous requirements, implicit assumptions, missing constraints, scope boundaries, unresolved questions\n   120→\n   121→### Input Preservation (before producing clarification)\n   122→\n   123→1. Glob `.wazir/input/tasks/*.md`. If files exist:\n   124→   - Adopt those specs as the starting point — copy content verbatim into the clarification's item descriptions.\n   125→   - Enhance with codebase scan + research findings. **Never remove detail — only add.**\n   126→   - Every acceptance criterion from input must appear verbatim.\n   127→   - Every API endpoint, color hex code, and UI dimension from input must appear in the relevant item section.\n   128→2. If `.wazir/input/tasks/` is empty or missing, synthesize from `briefing.md` alone.\n   129→\n   130→### Informed Question Batching (after research, before producing clarification)\n   131→\n   132→Research has completed. You now have codebase context and external findings. Before producing the clarification, ask the user INFORMED questions — informed by the research, not guesses.\n   133→\n   134→**Rules:**\n   135→1. **Research runs FIRST, questions come AFTER.** Never ask questions before research completes.\n   136→2. **Batch questions:** 1-3 batches of 3-7 questions each. Never one-at-a-time.\n   137→3. **Every scope exclusion must be explicitly confirmed by the user.** You MUST NOT decide that something is \"out of scope\" without asking. If the input doesn't mention docs, ask: \"The input doesn't mention documentation — should we include API docs, or is that explicitly out of scope?\" Do NOT assume.\n   138→4. **If the input is clear and complete:** Zero questions is fine. State: \"Input is clear and specific. No ambiguities detected. Proceeding with clarification.\"\n   139→5. **In auto mode (`interaction_mode: auto`):** Questions go to the gating agent, not the user.\n   140→6. **In interactive mode (`interaction_mode: interactive`):** More detailed questions, present research findings that informed each question.\n   141→\n   142→**Question format:**\n   143→```\n   144→Based on research, I have [N] questions before proceeding:\n   145→\n   146→**Scope & Intent**\n   147→1. [Question informed by research finding]\n   148→2. [Question about ambiguous requirement]\n   149→\n   150→**Technical Decisions**\n   151→3. [Question about architecture choice discovered during research]\n   152→4. [Question about dependency/framework preference]\n   153→\n   154→**Boundaries**\n   155→5. [Explicit scope boundary question — \"Should X be included or excluded?\"]\n   156→```\n   157→\n   158→Ask via AskUserQuestion with the full batch. Wait for answers. If answers introduce new ambiguity, ask a follow-up batch (max 3 batches total).\n   159→\n   160→### Clarification Production\n   161→\n   162→Read the briefing, research brief, user answers to questions, and codebase context. Produce:\n   163→\n   164→- **What** we're building — concrete deliverables\n   165→- **Why** — the motivation and business value\n   166→- **Constraints** — technical, timeline, dependencies\n   167→- **Assumptions** — what we're taking as given (each explicitly confirmed by user or clearly stated in input)\n   168→- **Scope boundaries** — what's IN and what's explicitly OUT (every exclusion must reference the user's confirmation: \"Out of scope per user confirmation in question batch 1, Q5\")\n   169→- **Unresolved questions** — anything still ambiguous after question batches\n   170→\n   171→Save to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/clarification.md`.\n   172→\n   173→Invoke `wz:reviewer --mode clarification-review`. Resolve findings before presenting to user.\n   174→\n   175→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   176→\n   177→> **Clarification complete.**\n   178→>\n   179→> **Found:** [N] ambiguities resolved, [N] assumptions documented, [N] scope boundaries defined, [N] items explicitly marked out-of-scope\n   180→>\n   181→> **Without this phase:** Implementation would proceed with hidden assumptions, scope would creep mid-build, and acceptance criteria would be vague enough to pass any implementation\n   182→>\n   183→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of resolved ambiguities — e.g., \"clarified auth means OAuth2 with Google provider only\", \"out-of-scope: mobile responsive for v1\"]\n   184→\n   185→### Checkpoint: Clarification Review\n   186→\n   187→> **Here's the clarified scope:**\n   188→>\n   189→> [Full clarification]\n   190→\n   191→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   192→- **Question:** \"Does the clarified scope accurately capture what you want to build?\"\n   193→- **Options:**\n   194→  1. \"Approved — continue to spec hardening\" *(Recommended)*\n   195→  2. \"Needs changes — let me provide corrections\"\n   196→  3. \"Missing important context — let me add information\"\n   197→\n   198→Wait for the user's selection before continuing. Route feedback: plan corrections → `user-feedback.md`, new requirements → `briefing.md`.\n   199→\n   200→---\n   201→\n   202→## Sub-Workflow 3: Spec Harden (specify + spec-challenge workflows)\n   203→\n   204→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   205→\n   206→> **Spec Hardening** — About to convert the clarified scope into a measurable, testable specification and then run adversarial spec-challenge review to find gaps.\n   207→>\n   208→> **Why this matters:** Without hardening, acceptance criteria stay vague (\"it should work well\") instead of measurable (\"response time under 200ms for 95th percentile\"). Vague specs pass any implementation, making review meaningless.\n   209→>\n   210→> **Looking for:** Untestable criteria, missing error handling specs, undefined edge cases, performance requirements, security constraints\n   211→\n   212→Delegate to the specify workflow (`workflows/specify.md`):\n   213→\n   214→1. Loop runs for `pass_counts[depth]` passes.\n   217→\n   218→Save result to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/spec-hardened.md`.\n   219→\n   220→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   221→\n   222→> **Spec Hardening complete.**\n   223→>\n   224→> **Found:** [N] acceptance criteria tightened, [N] edge cases added, [N] error handling requirements specified, [N] spec-challenge findings resolved\n   225→>\n   226→> **Without this phase:** Acceptance criteria would be subjective, review would have no concrete standard to measure against, and \"done\" would mean whatever the implementer decided\n   227→>\n   228→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of hardening changes — e.g., \"added 404 handling spec for missing resources\", \"specified max payload size of 5MB\", \"added rate limit requirement of 100 req/min\"]\n   229→\n   230→### Content-Author Detection\n   231→\n   232→After spec hardening, scan the spec for content needs. Auto-enable the `author` workflow if the spec mentions any of:\n   233→- Database seeding, seed data, fixtures, sample records\n   234→- Sample content, placeholder text, demo data\n   235→- Test fixtures, mock API responses, test data files\n   236→- Translations, i18n strings, localization\n   237→- Copy (button labels, error messages, onboarding text)\n   238→- Documentation content, user guides, API docs\n   239→- Email templates, notification text\n   240→\n   241→If detected, set `workflow_policy.author.enabled = true` in the run config and note:\n   242→> **Content needs detected.** The content-author workflow will run after design approval to produce: [list detected content types].\n   243→\n   244→### Checkpoint: Hardened Spec Review\n   245→\n   246→> **Spec hardened. Changes made:**\n   247→>\n   248→> [List of gaps found and how they were tightened]\n   249→\n   250→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   251→- **Question:** \"Are the spec hardening changes acceptable?\"\n   252→- **Options:**\n   253→  1. \"Approved — continue to brainstorming\" *(Recommended)*\n   254→  2. \"Disagree with a change — let me specify\"\n   255→  3. \"Found more gaps — let me add\"\n   256→\n   257→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   258→\n   259→---\n   260→\n   261→## Sub-Workflow 4: Brainstorm (design + design-review workflows)\n   262→\n   263→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   264→\n   265→> **Brainstorming** — About to propose 2-3 design approaches with explicit trade-offs, then run design-review on the approved choice.\n   266→>\n   267→> **Why this matters:** Without exploring alternatives, the first approach that comes to mind gets built — even if a simpler, more maintainable, or more performant option exists. This is where architectural mistakes get caught cheaply instead of discovered during implementation.\n   268→>\n   269→> **Looking for:** Architectural trade-offs, scalability implications, complexity vs. simplicity, alignment with existing codebase patterns\n   270→\n   271→Invoke the `brainstorming` skill (`wz:brainstorming`):\n   272→\n   273→1. Propose 2-3 viable approaches with explicit trade-offs\n   274→2. For each approach: effort estimate, risk assessment, what it enables/prevents\n   275→3. Recommend one approach with rationale\n   276→\n   277→### Checkpoint: Design Approval\n   278→\n   279→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   280→- **Question:** \"Which design approach should we implement?\"\n   281→- **Options:**\n   282→  1. \"Approach A — [one-line summary]\" *(Recommended)*\n   283→  2. \"Approach B — [one-line summary]\"\n   284→  3. \"Approach C — [one-line summary]\"\n   285→  4. \"Modify an approach — let me specify changes\"\n   286→\n   287→Wait for the user's selection before continuing. This is the most important checkpoint.\n   288→\n   289→Save approved design to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/design.md`.\n   290→\n   291→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   292→\n   293→> **Brainstorming complete.**\n   294→>\n   295→> **Found:** [N] approaches evaluated, [N] trade-offs documented, [N] design-review findings resolved\n   296→>\n   297→> **Without this phase:** The first viable approach would be built without considering alternatives — potentially choosing a complex solution when a simple one exists, or an approach that conflicts with existing patterns\n   298→>\n   299→> **Changed because of this work:** [Selected approach and why, rejected alternatives and why, design-review adjustments made]\n   300→\n   301→After approval: design-review loop with `--mode design-review` (5 canonical dimensions: spec coverage, design-spec consistency, accessibility, visual consistency, exported-code fidelity).\n   302→\n   303→---\n   304→\n   305→## Sub-Workflow 5: Plan (plan + plan-review workflows)\n   306→\n   307→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   308→\n   309→> **Planning** — About to break the approved design into ordered, dependency-aware implementation tasks with a gap analysis against the original input.\n   310→>\n   311→> **Why this matters:** Without explicit planning, tasks get implemented in the wrong order (breaking dependencies), items from the input get silently dropped, and task granularity is either too coarse (monolithic changes that are hard to review) or too fine (overhead without value).\n   312→>\n   313→> **Looking for:** Correct dependency ordering, complete input coverage, appropriate task granularity, clear acceptance criteria per task\n   314→\n   315→Delegate to `wz:writing-plans`:\n   316→\n   317→1. Planner produces a SINGLE execution plan at `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/execution-plan.md` in spec-kit format.\n   318→2. **Gap analysis exit gate:** Compare original input against plan. Invoke `wz:reviewer --mode plan-review`.\n   319→3. Loop until clean or cap reached.\n   320→\n   321→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   322→\n   323→> **Planning complete.**\n   324→>\n   325→> **Found:** [N] tasks created, [N] dependencies mapped, [N] plan-review findings resolved, [N] gap analysis items addressed\n   326→>\n   327→> **Without this phase:** Tasks would be implemented in ad-hoc order breaking dependencies, input items would be silently dropped, and task sizes would vary wildly making review inconsistent\n   328→>\n   329→> **Changed because of this work:** [Task count, dependency chain summary, any items reordered or split during plan-review]\n   330→\n   331→### Checkpoint: Plan Review\n   332→\n   333→> **Implementation plan: [N] tasks**\n   334→>\n   335→> | # | Task | Complexity | Dependencies | Description |\n   336→> |---|------|-----------|--------------|-------------|\n   337→\n   338→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   339→- **Question:** \"Does the implementation plan look correct and complete?\"\n   340→- **Options:**\n   341→  1. \"Approved — ready for execution\" *(Recommended)*\n   342→  2. \"Reorder or split tasks\"\n   343→  3. \"Missing tasks\"\n   344→  4. \"Too granular / too coarse\"\n   345→\n   346→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   347→\n   348→---\n   349→\n   350→### Scope Coverage Gate (Hard Gate)\n   351→\n   352→Before presenting the plan to the user, verify ALL input items are covered:\n   353→\n   354→1. Count distinct items/deliverables in the input briefing (`.wazir/input/briefing.md` + any `input/*.md` files)\n   355→2. Count tasks in the execution plan\n   356→3. **If `tasks_in_plan < items_in_input`:** STOP and present:\n   357→\n   358→> **Scope reduction detected.** The input contains [N] items but the plan only covers [M].\n   359→>\n   360→> Missing items: [list]\n   361→\n   362→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   363→- **Question:** \"The plan is missing [N-M] items from your input. How should we proceed?\"\n   364→- **Options:**\n   365→  1. \"Add missing items to the plan\" *(Recommended)*\n   366→  2. \"Approve reduced scope — I confirm these items can be dropped\"\n   367→\n   368→**The clarifier MUST NOT autonomously drop items into \"future tiers\", \"deferred\", or \"out of scope\" without explicit user approval. This is a hard rule.**\n   369→\n   370→Invariant: `items_in_plan >= items_in_input` unless user explicitly approves reduction.\n   371→\n   372→---\n   373→\n   374→## Reasoning Output\n   375→\n   376→Throughout the clarifier phase, produce reasoning at two layers:\n   377→\n   378→### User Output: Before Research\n   379→\n   380→```\n   381→I'm about to research your request. Here's what I need to figure out:\n   382→1. [specific thing] — because [why it matters for YOUR request]\n   383→2. [specific thing] — because [risk if we skip this]\n   384→3. [specific thing] — because [what could go wrong]\n   385→```\n   386→\n   387→### User Output: After Research\n   388→\n   389→```\n   390→Research complete. Here's what I found and why it matters:\n   391→1. [finding] — this means [impact on your project]\n   392→   Without this: [what would have gone wrong]\n   393→2. [finding] — this changes [specific decision]\n   394→   Without this: [concrete mistake avoided]\n   395→```\n   396→\n   397→### User Output: Before Clarification Questions\n   398→\n   399→```\n   400→I have [N] questions before we proceed. These aren't bureaucratic — each one prevents a specific mistake:\n   401→1. [question] — asking because [what goes wrong if I assume]\n   402→2. [question] — asking because [concrete risk]\n   403→```\n   404→\n   405→### User Output: Between Sub-Workflows\n   406→\n   407→```\n   408→[Previous workflow] complete. Moving to [next workflow] because [concrete reason].\n   409→Key input from previous step: [what carries forward and why it matters].\n   410→```\n   411→\n   412→**File (Layer 2):** Write `.wazir/runs/<id>/reasoning/phase-clarifier-reasoning.md` with structured entries per decision:\n   413→- **Trigger** — what prompted the decision\n   414→- **Options considered** — alternatives evaluated\n   415→- **Chosen** — selected option\n   416→- **Reasoning** — why\n   417→- **Confidence** — high/medium/low\n   418→- **Counterfactual** — what would go wrong without this info\n   419→\n   420→Examples of clarifier reasoning entries:\n   421→- \"Trigger: input says 'auth' without specifying provider. Options: ask user, assume OAuth2, assume magic links. Chosen: ask user.
